“The arousers.” Those who were saying (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 44:24" href="/Psalms.44.24"><i>Ps</i>. 44:24</a>): “Be roused, why do You sleep, o Eternal, etc.” Does there exist sleep before the Omnipresent? Has it not already been said (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 121:4" href="/Psalms.121.4"><i>Ps</i>. 121:4</a>): “Lo, He will not slumber nor sleep, the Guardian of Israel!” Why does the verse say (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 78:65" href="/Psalms.78.65"><i>Ps</i>. 78:65</a>): “Like a sleeper awoke the Eternal, like a hero exhilarated by wine.” But in a symbolic way it is as if sleep were before Him when Israel is in trouble and the other peoples are at ease. So it says (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Job 17:2" href="/Job.17.2"><i>Job</i> 17:2</a>): “When they apostasize, My Eye will rest.”
“The hitters.” Those who were hitting the calf between its horns. Joḥanan the High Priest said to them, how long will you feed torn animals to the altar? He went and made them rings. Rebbi Abba in the name of Rebbi Jehudah: He made rings for them, wide below and narrow at the top.
“Up to his days the hammer was hitting in Jerusalem,” up to his early days. “And in his days nobody had to ask about <i>demay</i>” because he sent out teams
The word of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi implies some are censure and some praise. Since Rebbi Yose said in the name of Rebbi Tanḥum bar Ḥiyya, Rebbi Ḥizqiah, Rebbi Eleazar ben Rebbi Yose, Rebbi Tanḥum, Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi, originally tithe was split into three parts. One third to his acquaintances among Cohanim and Levites, one third to the public treasury, one third to the poor and the fellows in Jerusalem. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said, a person who went to court in Jerusalem, up to three letters he paid for himself, from there on from the public treasury. When Eleazar ben Paḥora and Judah ben Pakora came, they took it by force and it would have been in his hand to stop this but he did not but disestablished the declaration of tithes, and this is for censure. But the arousers for praise and the hitters for praise.
“Up to his days the hammer was hitting in Jerusalem,” up to his early days. Rebbi Ḥasida asked Rebbi Ḥizqiah, is it not reasonable to the end of his days. He said, I also am of that opinion.
{What means] <i>demay?</i> Rebbi Yose in the name of Rebbi Abbahu, Rebbi Ḥizqiah in the name of Rebbi Jehudah ben Pazi: Maybe he put in order, maybe he did not put in order.

Halakhah 12

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> When the Synhedrion was disestablished<sup class="footnote-marker">189</sup><i class="footnote">Not really disestablished but when criminal jurisdiction was taken away from Jewish courts, transferred to the Roman administration, and only strictly religious matters were left to the High Court which was generally regarded as Synhedrion.</i>, the epithalamium stopped at wedding feasts as it was said<sup class="footnote-marker">190</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Isaiah 24:9" href="/Isaiah.24.9"><i>Is.</i> 24:9</a>.</i>: “They shall not drink wine in song.”
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> Abba bar Rav Jeremiah said: “The Elders are no longer at the gate<sup class="footnote-marker">191</sup><i class="footnote"><i>Thr.</i> 5:14: “The Elders are no longer at the gate, [therefore not] the young men at their songs.” The same in the Babli, 48a, in the name of Rav Huna ben Rav Joshua, 2 generations after Abba bar Rav Jeremiah.</i>” etc.
Rav Ḥisda said, in earlier times the fear of the court was on them and they did not include lewd language in song. But now when the fear of the court is no longer on them they include lewd language in song<sup class="footnote-marker">192</sup><i class="footnote">Lewd language being a regular feature of the Greek epithalamium.</i>.
In earlier times they required payment only from a person alone. But now they require payment from him and his family<sup class="footnote-marker">195</sup><i class="footnote">In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 15:7" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).15.7">Tosephta, 15:7</a>, this is combined with the verse <a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 20:5" href="/Leviticus.20.5"><i>Lev.</i> 20:5</a>, alluded to later. A court punishes only the criminal but God’s justice is against “that man (who sacrifices his children to the Moloch) and his family.” This proves that if the courts can no longer enforce biblical law, the Heavenly Court will enforce it in a much harsher way.</i>. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Abun said in the name of Rav Ḥuna: In earlier times, for every trouble that came over the community they have a joyous occasion to make up for it<sup class="footnote-marker">196</sup><i class="footnote">The delivery from trouble was a festive occasion documented in <i>Megillat Ta‘anit,</i> the catalogue of days when fasting was forbidden. But now, in the words of the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 15:6" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).15.6">Tosephta (15:6</a>): Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel says, for every trouble that comes over the community, the court disestablishes another joyous occasion.</i>. But after the Synhedrion was abolished, song disappeared from wedding feasts. After both disappeared, <sup class="footnote-marker">197</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Lamentations 5:15" href="/Lamentations.5.15"><i>Thr.</i> 5:15</a>.</i>“our heart’s joy stopped, our dance turned into mourning.” But what was the high court good for<sup class="footnote-marker">198</sup><i class="footnote">What is the connection between the disestablishment of Jewish criminal jurisdiction and the disappearance of the epithalamium from Jewish weddings? The rest of the paragraph has a close parallel in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 15:7" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).15.7">Tosephta 15:7</a>.</i>? But because it was said<sup class="footnote-marker">199</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Leviticus 20:4" href="/Leviticus.20.4"><i>Lev.</i> 20:4</a>. It is implied that the real reason is the following v. 5.</i> “if the people of the Land consistently turn away their eyes from that man when he is giving of his seed to the Moloch, not to kill him,” in any death they would choose<sup class="footnote-marker">200</sup><i class="footnote">This gives the high court emergency powers to act as a secret, Vehmic, court in case the criminal is too powerful.</i>. They gave a parable, to what can this be compared? To one who was a criminal in a town. They delivered him to the one wielding reeds, who jailed him, but he turned out to be stronger than the one wielding reeds. They delivered him to the one wielding sticks who hit him, but he turned out to be stronger than the one wielding sticks<sup class="footnote-marker">201</sup><i class="footnote">He might be the Roman lictor since the ruler mentioned is a Roman proconsul.</i>. They delivered him to the wielder of leather straps who whipped him, but he turned out to be stronger than the wielder of leather straps. They delivered him to the ruler who hung him in the kiln<sup class="footnote-marker">202</sup><i class="footnote">Greek κάμινος, ἡ, “oven, furnace, kiln.”</i>. So the later troubles cause the earlier ones to be forgotten.

Halakhah 13

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> After the earlier prophets died, Urim and Tummim<sup class="footnote-marker">203</sup><i class="footnote">The oracle carried by the High Priest.</i> stopped. When the Temple was destroyed, the <i>shamir</i> and flowing bee’s honey stopped and trusting men disappeared, as it was said<sup class="footnote-marker">204</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 12:2" href="/Psalms.12.2"><i>Ps.</i> 12:2</a>.</i>: “Help, o Eternal, for the pious man is finished, for the trusting have vanished from mankind.”
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “After the earlier prophets died, Urim and Tummim stopped.” Rebbi Samuel bar Naḥman in the name of Rebbi Jonathan: These are Samuel and David<sup class="footnote-marker">205</sup><i class="footnote">Since there is no explicit reference in Scripture about priestly oracles in books later than <i>Samuel.</i> In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 48b" href="/Sotah.48b">Babli, 48b</a>, this is the opinion of Rav Huna, the most prominent of Rav’s students.</i>. Rebbi Abba bar Cahana in the name of Rav: These are Gad and Nathan<sup class="footnote-marker">206</sup><i class="footnote">David’s court prophets.</i>. Rebbi Jeremiah, Rebbi Samuel bar Isaac in the name of Rav: These are Jeremiah and Barukh. The word of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi implies that these are Jeremiah and Barukh. For Rebbi Joshua ben Levi said<sup class="footnote-marker">207</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="II Chronicles 26:5" href="/II_Chronicles.26.5"><i>2Chr.</i> 26:5</a>. The quote proves that oracles were used by kings after David (even though Zacariah is not mentioned in the list of high priests in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezra 7" href="/Ezra.7"><i>Ezra</i> 7</a> and Urim and Tummim were high-priestly oracles), as pointed out in the Babli by Rabba bar Samuel, a slightly younger contemporary of R. Joshua ben Levi. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 13:3" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).13.3">Tosephta, 13:3</a>, states that the oracle disappeared only with the destruction of the first Temple. In many quotes in Babli and Yerushalmi (e. g., <i>Ta‘aniot</i> 2:1 65a line 64, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Yoma 21b" href="/Yoma.21b">Yoma 21b</a>) the oracle is mentioned in the list of five things missing in the second Temple.</i>, “it was when he asked God in the days of Zacariah who understood God’s visions.”
After the last prophets, Haggai, Zacariah, and Malachi, died, the Holy Ghost stopped from them, but nevertheless they were using the disembodied voice<sup class="footnote-marker">209</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 13:3" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).13.3">Tosephta 13:3</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 48b" href="/Sotah.48b">Babli 48b</a>. In the Tosephta: “nevertheless they (the Heavenly Court) were communicating the disembodied voice.”</i>. If happened that Simeon the Just heard a disembodied voice coming out of the holiest-of-holies saying: Gaius Caligula was killed and his decisions became void.<sup class="footnote-marker">210</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 13:6" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).13.6">Tosephta 13:6</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 33a" href="/Sotah.33a">Babli 33a</a>. At least one of the names mentioned here cannot be correct.</i> It happened that young men went to fight at Antiochia when Joḥanan the High Priest heard a disembodied voice coming out of the holiest-of-holies saying: The young people are victorious who fought at Antiochia. At that time they wrote down the exact time and found that it happened exactly at that hour<sup class="footnote-marker">211</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 13:5" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).13.5">Tosephta 13:5</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 33a" href="/Sotah.33a">Babli 33a</a>. It was remarked that the voice spoke Aramaic which is not understood by angels.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">212</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 13:3-4" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).13.3-4">Tosephta 13:3–4</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 48b" href="/Sotah.48b">Babli 48b</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sanhedrin 11a" href="/Sanhedrin.11a"><i>Sanhedrin</i> 11a</a>, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 57a" href="/Berakhot.57a"><i>Berakhot</i> 57a</a>; Yerushalmi <i>Avodah zarah</i> 3:1 (42c 1. 32), <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Horayot 3:4:2-5:16" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Horayot.3.4.2-5.16"><i>Horaiot</i> 3:7</a> (48c 1. 41).</i> It happened that Elders came together in the house Gadia<sup class="footnote-marker">213</sup><i class="footnote">In both Babli sources: Guriah.</i> in Jericho, when a disembodied voice came and said to them: There is among you one man who would be worthy that the Holy Spirit should rest on him<sup class="footnote-marker">214</sup><i class="footnote">That he should be a prophet.</i>, only the generation is not worthy. They all looked at Hillel the Elder. When he died, they said about him, o meek, pious student of Ezra. Again it happened that Elders came together in a second floor at Jabne, when a disembodied voice came and said to them: There is among you one man who would be worthy that the Holy Spirit should rest on him, only the generation is not worthy. They all looked at Samuel Minor. Why was he called Minor? Because he effaced himself. Some say, because he was slightly below Samuel from Ramah<sup class="footnote-marker">215</sup><i class="footnote">The biblical prophet.</i>. When he died, they said about him o meek, pious student of Hillel the Elder. When he was dying he said<sup class="footnote-marker">216</sup><i class="footnote">It is clear that Samuel Minor lived in the time of Gamliel I, Hillel’s grandson, and that there already was an academy at Jabneh at that time.</i>: Simeon and Ismael<sup class="footnote-marker">217</sup><i class="footnote">Simeon ben Gamliel, president of the revolutionary government in the war of 68–70, and Ismael, the High Priest during the revolt; both executed after Titus’s triumph in Rome. (Late and secondary transformation of this source: <i>Mekhilta dR. Ismael Mišpaṭim</i>18, <i>Šemaḥot</i> 8).</i> to the word, the rest of the people to plunder, immense troubles will be. He said that in Aramaic and they did not understand what he was saying. For Rebbi Jehudah ben Baba they intended to say o meek, pious, but the time was torn<sup class="footnote-marker">218</sup><i class="footnote">He was executed in the aftermath of the war of Bar Kokhba.</i>.
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">219</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 15:1" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).15.1">Tosephta 15:1</a> the entire paragraph. The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 48b" href="/Sotah.48b">Babli, 48b</a>, quotes only the part referring to R. Jehudah’s statement, and that anonymously.<br>In many places, the <i>shamir</i> is listed as a creature whose existence was part of the plan of Creation but which came into being only at its appointed time (the expression being: it was created Friday evening at dusk): Mishnah <i>Abot</i>5:6, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Pesachim 54a" href="/Pesachim.54a">Babli <i>Pesaḥim</i> 54a</a>, <i>Sifry Deut.</i> 355, <i>Mekhilta Bešallaḥ Wayyissa‘</i> 5, <i>Abot dR. Nathan B</i> 37, <i>Pirqe R. Eliezer</i>19,31, <i>Tanḥuma Wayyera</i> 23, <i>Pseudo-Jonathan Num.</i> 22:28, <i>Midraš Ma‘aśeh</i><br><i>Torah</i> (Jellinek vol. 2, p. 100). Cf. also the story of Solomon and the shamir in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Gittin 68b" href="/Gittin.68b">Babli <i>Giṭṭin</i> 68b</a>.</i>: Rebbi Jehudah said, what was this <i>shamir?</i> It is a creature that existed from the creation of the world and if one shows it stones those would open themselves like the two boards of a <i>pinax</i><sup class="footnote-marker">220</sup><i class="footnote">A writing tablet of two smooth wooden plates hinged together and covered with wax. Greek πίναξ, - ακος, ὁ, “board, plank, anything made of wood; writing tablet, catalogs, etc.”</i>, and Solomon built the Temple with it. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">221</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 6:7" href="/I_Kings.6.7"><i>1K.</i> 6:7</a>.</i>: “During the building of the House, it was built from whole carried stones, and hammers or axe or any iron implement was not heard in the House when it was built.” Rebbi Nehemiah says, they were sawed. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">222</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="I Kings 7:9" href="/I_Kings.7.9"><i>1K.</i> 7:9</a>.</i>: “All these were expensive stones, in the measure of ashlars, sawed with a saw inside and out.” Say now, at the building site they were not treated at all but they were finished outside and then brought inside<sup class="footnote-marker">223</sup><i class="footnote">Since iron may not be used in the building of the Temple, <i>Ex.</i> 20:25.</i>. Rebbi says, the words of Rebbi Jehudah are convincing for the stones of the Temple and those of Rebbi Nehemiah for the stones of Solomon’s palace. But since nothing can withstand it, and even when it was put on a stone or a box sheet it would split it and fall down, what did they do to restrain it? One was binding it with wool fibers and put it into a lead cylinder filled with barley bran. That is what is written<sup class="footnote-marker">224</sup><i class="footnote">Am. 5:9; this is taken as referring to the shamir.</i>: “He enjoys robbing the strong.”
“And flowing bee’s honey”. Rebbi Eleazar said, honey that comes with floaters. Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Ḥanina said, farina which floats on the sieve kneaded with honey and butter<sup class="footnote-marker">225</sup><i class="footnote">He explains the recipe R. Eleazar had in mind, as a delicacy which lost its taste with the destruction of the first Temple. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 48b" href="/Sotah.48b">Babli 48b</a>, in the name of Rav.</i>. <sup class="footnote-marker">226</sup><i class="footnote">This is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 1:8:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.1.8.7">Chapter 1, Note 298</a>; explained in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Peah 7:3:11" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Peah.7.3.11"><i>Peah</i> Chapter 7, Notes 71–75</a>.</i> Rebbi Joḥanan said, the second quality fruit we ate in our youth tasted better that the peaches we ate in our old age, because during his lifetime the world changed. Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba said, one <i>seah</i> of Arbel grain did yield one <i>seah</i> of fine flour, one <i>seah</i> of white flour, one <i>seah</i> of dark flour, one <i>seah</i> of bran, one <i>seah</i> of coarse bran. But today, we do not even get one for one.
“Trusting men disappeared.” Rebbi Ze‘ira said, men who trusted in Torah, as one teacher who was teaching Bible to his brother in Tyre when they were calling on him for a business deal<sup class="footnote-marker">227</sup><i class="footnote">Greek πραγματεία, ἡ, “occupation, business, diligent study, prosecution of business”.</i>. He said, I do not push aside my set time<sup class="footnote-marker">228</sup><i class="footnote">Time set aside for study every day at the same hour.</i>. If it is destined to come to me, it will come to me<sup class="footnote-marker">229</sup><i class="footnote">This essentially disproves the Mishnah that there are no longer people trusting in God.</i>.

Halakhah 14

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel says in the name of Rebbi Joshua: Since the day the Temple was destroyed there is no day without a curse, and the dew did not descend for a blessing; and the taste of fruits disappeared. Rebbi Yose says, also the fat of fruits disappeared.<br>Rebbi Simeon ben Eleazar says, purity<sup class="footnote-marker">230</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning: lack of purity, the fact that people eat their profane food not under the rules of ritual purity applying to sanctified food, the original distinguishing feature of the old pharisaic sect.</i> took away taste, tithes<sup class="footnote-marker">231</sup><i class="footnote">The fact that people did not tithe but mostly only gave heave; cf. Tractate <i>Demay</i>.</i> took away the fat of grain, immorality and sorcery killed everything<sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote">Moral, not ritual, defects account for all other troubles. The Babylonian Mishnah essentially is the Tosephta, cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 9:14:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.9.14.2">Note 236</a>.</i>.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> It is written<sup class="footnote-marker">233</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Psalms 7:12" href="/Psalms.7.12"><i>Ps</i>. 7:12</a>.</i>: “But God is angry every day.” Rebbi Ze‘ira said, the earlier ones<sup class="footnote-marker">234</sup><i class="footnote">The troubles are cumulative; the new troubles do not eliminate the old ones.</i> all continue. What can do away with them<sup class="footnote-marker">235</sup><i class="footnote">The earlier troubles?</i>? Rebbi Abin in the name of Rebbi Aḥa: The priestly blessing does away with them. <sup class="footnote-marker">236</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 15:2" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).15.2">Tosephta 15:2</a>; there the text of the Mishnah also is repeated.</i> Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel said, you can observe that dew has become cursed. In earlier times, a village abundant in dew was abundant in produce but today, a village abundant in dew is poor in produce<sup class="footnote-marker">237</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Peah 7:3:7" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Peah.7.3.7"><i>Peah</i> 7:4, Notes 66</a> ff.</i>! In earlier times, dew descended on chaff and straw and whitened it<sup class="footnote-marker">238</sup><i class="footnote">In the Tosephta, his proof is from the manna which was made shiny by the dew on it.</i>, but today it descends on chaff and straw and blackens it.
It was stated<sup class="footnote-marker">239</sup><i class="footnote">Text of the Babylonian Mishnah. In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 15:2" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).15.2">Tosephta 15:2</a>: “tithes took away oils and grain.”</i>: “Rebbi Simeon ben Eleazar says, purity<sup class="footnote-marker">230</sup><i class="footnote">Meaning: lack of purity, the fact that people eat their profane food not under the rules of ritual purity applying to sanctified food, the original distinguishing feature of the old pharisaic sect.</i> took away taste and smell, tithes<sup class="footnote-marker">231</sup><i class="footnote">The fact that people did not tithe but mostly only gave heave; cf. Tractate <i>Demay</i>.</i> took away the fat of grain.” From what was taken most? Rebbi Levi ben Ḥaita said, let us hear from the following<sup class="footnote-marker">240</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Haggai 2:16" href="/Haggai.2.16"><i>Ḥag</i>. 2:16</a>. Grain shrank from 1 to .5 but wine from 1 to .4, which is 20% less.</i>: “One thought to come to a heap of twenty and it was ten. He came to the winepress to draw 50 pitchers,” it does not say ‘and there were 25’ but “and there were 20.” “<sup class="footnote-marker">241</sup><i class="footnote">This is the version of the Babylonian Mishnah.</i> But the Sages say, immorality and sorcery killed everything<sup class="footnote-marker">232</sup><i class="footnote">Moral, not ritual, defects account for all other troubles. The Babylonian Mishnah essentially is the Tosephta, cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 9:14:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.9.14.2">Note 236</a>.</i>.”

Halakhah 15

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> During Vespasian’s war<sup class="footnote-marker">242</sup><i class="footnote">The Jewish war which resulted in the destruction of the Temple.</i> they decided about<sup class="footnote-marker">243</sup><i class="footnote">The rabbinic High Court, reconstituted at Jabneh under Vespasian’s protection by the anti-war leader Joḥanan ben Zakkai forbade grooms to wear crowns as a sign of national mourning.</i> grooms’ crowns and the <i>erus</i><sup class="footnote-marker">244</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babli, this is defined as “one-sided percussion instrument;” in the interpretation of the Gaonim and <i>Arukh</i> a tymbal or tambourine. The Yerushalmi explanation is unintelligible.</i>. During Quietus’s<sup class="footnote-marker">245</sup><i class="footnote">The Jewish revolt against Trajan, outside the Land of Israel. קיטוס instead of טיטוס is the reading of the Geniza mss. of the Mishnah, of the Palestinian Mishnah (Cambridge ms.), and the Kaufman ms., of important mss. of <i>Seder ‘Olam</i> (cf. the author’s edition, Northvale NJ 1998, p. 260 ff.), and of a Gaonic responsum (<i>Ginze Schechter</i> 2, No. 17, p. 244, 249). That reading has been chosen for the translation. Cf. H. Graetz, <i>Geschichte der Juden</i><sup class="footnote-marker">3</sup>, vol. 4, <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sotah 9:1:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sotah.9.1.2">Note 14</a>.</i> war they decided about brides’ crowns and that nobody should teach Greek to his son<sup class="footnote-marker">246</sup><i class="footnote">The <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 49b" href="/Sotah.49b">Babli, 49b</a>, dates the prohibition of Greek to the time of Pompey.</i>. During the last war they decided that a bride should not be carried in a litter through the city; our teachers<sup class="footnote-marker">247</sup><i class="footnote">In general, “our teachers” refers either to Rebbi, R. Jehudah I the Prince, or his grandson, R. Jehudah II the Prince. In any case, the last sentence is a post-Mishnaic correction of the Mishnah.</i> permitted that a bride should be carried in a litter through the city.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> “Our head’s crown fell”; these are the grooms’ crowns, that is gilded woolen strips. Rebbi Abba in the name of Rav: Of salt and sulfur<sup class="footnote-marker">249</sup><i class="footnote">In the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 49b" href="/Sotah.49b">Babli, 49b</a>, Rav holds that crowns of myrrh and roses are permitted, but of salt and sulfur prohibited. This is the tannaitic position in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 15:8" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).15.8">Tosephta 15:8</a>. Rashi explains that one makes a crown out of a solid rock of salt and uses sulfur to paint ornaments in gold color on the crown.</i>. Rav Jeremiah in the name of Rav: Of salt and olives. Rav Naḥman bar Jacob said, even of willows<sup class="footnote-marker">250</sup><i class="footnote">In the Babli, Samuel holds that crowns of salt rock are forbidden, of reeds or willows permitted, but Levi holds that even reeds and willows are forbidden.</i>. Rav Jeremiah of Šibšeb wore a crown of olive branches. Samuel heard this and said, it would have been better for him it he had been beheaded but not done this thing. That happened to him, as “an error coming from before the ruler.<sup class="footnote-marker">251</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ecclesiastes 10:5" href="/Ecclesiastes.10.5"><i>Eccl</i>. 10:5</a>.</i>”
The following are grooms’ chambers<sup class="footnote-marker">252</sup><i class="footnote">Here is missing a statement similar to <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 15:9" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).15.9">Tosephta 15:9</a>, hinted at in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 49b" href="/Sotah.49b">Babli 49b</a>: During the last war, they decided on grooms’ chambers (to forbid extravagant decorations of the bridal chamber.)</i>: Ornamented sheets on which hang golden halfmoons<sup class="footnote-marker">253</sup><i class="footnote">In the Tosephta: golden chambers. In the Babli: golden sheets.</i>. It was stated: But he makes papyrus<sup class="footnote-marker">254</sup><i class="footnote">The word אפיפיירות is discussed at length in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Kilayim 6:3:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Kilayim.6.3.1"><i>Kilaim</i> 6:3, Note 38</a>.</i> ropes and hangs on them anything he wants.
Mishnah: “And the <i>erus</i>.” <i>resisa</i><sup class="footnote-marker">255</sup><i class="footnote">In biblical Hebrew, this would mean “splinters”. Levy in his Dictionary conjectures that it refers to a musical instrument full of holes. Kohout proposes to amend to רביכה, a rebeq, a music instrument. It seems futile to try to explain the Yerushalmi in the light of the Babli. The word <i>erus</i> might be Accadic <i>erēšum</i> “smell, perfume” and רסיסה good Hebrew ריסוס “spraying (with perfume <i>erēšum ṭābum</i>)”.</i>.
The following are brides’ crowns, that is a city of gold<sup class="footnote-marker">256</sup><i class="footnote">A golden diadem in the shape of a city wall. The same explanation in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 49b" href="/Sotah.49b">Babli, 49b</a>. In the Tosephta, “a golden headband”.</i>. Rebbi Aqiba made for his wife a city of gold<sup class="footnote-marker">257</sup><i class="footnote">Reported also in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Shabbat 86a" href="/Shabbat.86a">Babli, <i>Šabbat</i> 86a</a>.</i>, which made Rabban Gamliel’s wife jealous. He said to her, did you ever do what she did? She sold her braided hair, gave the money to him so he could study Torah<sup class="footnote-marker">258</sup><i class="footnote">In the tradition of the Babli, she was a daughter from a very rich house who was disinherited for marrying an ignorant nobody. She had married him on condition that he would study to become a famous Sage.</i>.
<sup class="footnote-marker">260</sup><i class="footnote">This is from <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Peah 1:1:21" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Peah.1.1.21"><i>Peah</i> 1:1, Notes 94–97</a>. Cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Menachot 99b" href="/Menachot.99b">Babli <i>Menaḥot</i> 99b</a>.</i> They asked Rebbi Joshua: May a person teach Greek to his son? He said to them, he may teach him at an hour that is neither day nor night as it is written (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Joshua 1:8" href="/Joshua.1.8"><i>Jos</i>. 1:8</a>): “You shall meditate about it day and night.” If it is so, a man would be forbidden to teach a profession to his son since it is written: “You shall meditate about it day and night.” But Rebbi Ismael stated (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Deuteronomy 30:19" href="/Deuteronomy.30.19"><i>Deut</i>. 30:19</a>): “Choose life!” That refers to a profession. Rebbi Abba, son of Rebbi Ḥiyya bar Abba, Rebbi Ḥiyya in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: Because of informants. Rebbi Abbahu in the name of Rebbi Joḥanan: A person may teach Greek to his daughter since it is an ornament for her. Simeon bar Abba heard that and said: Because he wants to teach his daughters, he attaches it to Rebbi Joḥanan. It should come over me that I never heard it from Rebbi Joḥanan.
Who permits the earlier ones<sup class="footnote-marker">262</sup><i class="footnote">We find that “our teachers” permitted a prohibition dating from the war of Bar Kokhba. What is the status of the earlier decrees mentioned in the Mishnah.</i>? Rebbi Yose ben Rebbi Bun said, the one who permitted these permitted those<sup class="footnote-marker">263</sup><i class="footnote">He holds that “our teachers” abolished the entire Mishnah.</i>. As the following: The Head of the Diaspora sent and asked Rav Ḥisdai: what is the meaning of “taking away the head cover, removing the crown”<sup class="footnote-marker">264</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Ezekiel 21:31" href="/Ezekiel.21.31"><i>Ez</i>. 21:31</a>.</i>? He said to him, when the head cover was taken away, the crown was removed<sup class="footnote-marker">265</sup><i class="footnote">When the Temple was destroyed and the head cover of the High Priest (<a class="refLink" data-ref="Exodus 28:37" href="/Exodus.28.37"><i>Ex</i>. 28:37</a>) was taken away, then the grooms’ crowns should be removed. He found a biblical reason for the rabbinic decision.</i>. Rebbi Joḥanan heard this and said, he is grace and his words are gracious<sup class="footnote-marker">266</sup><i class="footnote">A parallel in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Gittin 7a" href="/Gittin.7a">Babli, <i>Giṭṭin</i> 7a</a>, based on the same etymological pun. A totally different interpretation of the verse, also endorsed by R. Joḥanan, in <i>Ruth rabba</i> 3(1).</i>.

Halakhah 16

<strong>MISHNAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">267</sup><i class="footnote">The Mishnah in the Babli is quite different in this first paragraph; it is close to the <i>baraita</i>/Tosephta quoted in the Halakhah as alternative version. The mention of Rebbi and R. Phineas ben Yaïr characterizes the entire Mishnah as a late addition.</i> When Rabban Joḥanan ben Zakkai died, the splendor of wisdom disappeared. When the elder Rabban Gamliel<sup class="footnote-marker">268</sup><i class="footnote">Hillel’s grandson, whom the Apostle Paul claimed as his teacher.</i> died, the honor of Torah disappeared, purity and self-discipline died. When Ismael ben Phiabi<sup class="footnote-marker">269</sup><i class="footnote">The last High Priest of good character.</i> died, the splendor of priesthood died. When Rebbi died, meekness and fear of sin died. When Rebbi Meїr died, the inventors of parables disappeared. When Rebbi Aqiba died, the preachers<sup class="footnote-marker">270</sup><i class="footnote">It may be that “interpreters of biblical verses” is meant. R. Aqiba is the last authority who systematically derived laws directly from an interpretation of verses.</i> disappeared. When Ben Azai died, the perseverers<sup class="footnote-marker">271</sup><i class="footnote">Who study day and night.</i> disappeared. When Ben Zoma died, the students<sup class="footnote-marker">272</sup><i class="footnote">It is difficult to know what this means. In the Babli, “the preachers disappeared”. Ben Zoma is known for his gnostic studies.</i> disappeared. When Rebbi Joshua died, good disappeared from the world<sup class="footnote-marker">273</sup><i class="footnote">Had he lived, he probably could have averted the uprising of Bar Kochba.</i> When Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah died, wealth disappeared from the Sages. When Rabban Gamliel died<sup class="footnote-marker">274</sup><i class="footnote">In many independent Mishnah mss. (and the following Tosephta) “Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel”; missing in the Babli. The Yerushalmi reading is preferable since Rabban Gamliel died just before the Bar Kochba revolt but his son died at the beginning of the Severan dynasty which was a good time for the Jewish population of Palestine.</i>, locusts came and troubles increased. When Rebbi Ḥanina ben Dosa and Yose the small<sup class="footnote-marker">275</sup><i class="footnote">קיטונתה is usually derived from Greek κοιτών “bedroom”, Syriac קיטונא “room”. In Babli and independent Mishnah he is called קטונתא “the little one”, because, according to some mss., he was the most insignificant of the pious. It is more than likely that the Yerushalmi קיטונתה is identical with קטונתא except for the addition of a stray י. This is accepted in the translation. Other Babli mss. and early medieval authors also call him “the concentrate of piety”.</i> died, piety disappeared. Why was he called Yose of the small room? For he was the concentrate of pious men. Rebbi Phineas ben Yaїr says, after the Temple was destroyed, fellows and freeborn were ashamed and covered their heads, people of [good] deeds shrivelled, strong-armed people and informers became dominant, nobody explains, nobody desires and nobody asks. On whom can we rely? On our Father in Heaven. The great Rebbi Eliezer<sup class="footnote-marker">276</sup><i class="footnote">R. Eliezer ben Hyrkanos.</i> says, from the day the Temple was destroyed, the Sages were diminished to be like scribes, the scribes like community servants, the community servants like common people; the common people go and degenerate, nobody desires and nobody asks. On whom can we rely? On our Father in Heaven.<br>On the heels of the Messiah impertinence will grow, inflation will lead, the vine will give its fruit but the wine will be expensive, the government will turn heretic<sup class="footnote-marker">277</sup><i class="footnote">This Mishnah expected the Messiah to appear when the Roman state turned Christian.</i>, nobody rebukes, the assembly hall will be a brothel, Galilee will be destroyed and Gaulanitis<sup class="footnote-marker">278</sup><i class="footnote">Which was densely settled by Jews in talmudic times, cf. <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Sheviit 6:1" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Sheviit.6.1"><i>Ševi‘it</i> 6:1, Notes 31–51</a>.</i> become deserted, frontier dwellers will move from city to city and nobody will have mercy on them, the wisdom of scholars will be defective, those who fear sin will be despised, truth will be absent, young men will insult Elders, Elders will stand before the young, “a son will abuse his father, a daughter rebel against her mother and a daughter-in-law against her mother-in-law, the enemies of a person are his family”<sup class="footnote-marker">279</sup><i class="footnote"><a class="refLink" data-ref="Micah 7:6" href="/Micah.7.6"><i>Micah</i> 7:6</a>.</i>, the generation is dog-faced, a son is not ashamed before his father. What do we have to rely on? Our Father in Heaven.
<strong>HALAKHAH:</strong> <sup class="footnote-marker">280</sup><i class="footnote">A similar version in <a class="refLink" data-ref="Tosefta Sotah (Lieberman) 15:3-5" href="/Tosefta_Sotah_(Lieberman).15.3-5">Tosephta 15:3–5</a>; <a class="refLink" data-ref="Sotah 49b" href="/Sotah.49b">Babli 49b</a>.</i>“When Rebbi Eliezer died, the book of wisdom was hidden<sup class="footnote-marker">281</sup><i class="footnote">In Tosephta and Babli: The Torah scroll was hidden.</i>. When Rebbi Joshua died, good counsel and good deeds disappeared from Israel. When Rebbi Aqiba died, the souces of wisdom disappeared. When Rebbi Eleazar ben Azariah died, wealth disappered from the Sages. When Rebbi Yose died, insight disappeared. When Ben Azai died, the perseverers disappeared. When Ben Zoma died, the preachers disappeared. When Rebbi Joshua died, good disappeared from the world. When Rebbi Ḥanina ben Dosa died, the workers [of wonders] disappeared. When Rebbi Yose the pious and Rebbi<sup class="footnote-marker">282</sup><i class="footnote">In the Tosephta sources, in the Babylonian <i>bardita,</i> and in a few Mishnah mss., he is called Abba Yose, placing him before the destruction of the Temple. In <a class="refLink" data-ref="Jerusalem Talmud Bava Kamma 3:7:2" href="/Jerusalem_Talmud_Bava_Kamma.3.7.2"><i>Baba qama</i> 3:7</a> (3d, 1. 37) he is called Yose the Babylonian or Yose ben Jehudah, without title.</i> Yose the minor died, pious men disappeared. Why is he called minor? For he was the concentrate of the just and the pious. When Rabban Simeon ben Gamliel died, locusts came and troubles increased. When Rebbi died, troubles were doubled.”
<sup class="footnote-marker">283</sup><i class="footnote">The entire paragraph is in <i>Avodah zarah</i> 3:1 (42c, 1. 42). The first sentence is also in the <a class="refLink" data-ref="Berakhot 28b" href="/Berakhot.28b">Babli, <i>Berakhot</i>28b</a>.</i> Rebbi Jacob bar Idi in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: When Rabban Joḥanan ben Zakkai died, he commanded and said, clear the courtyard because of the impurity and prepare a chair for Hezekiah, the king of Judah. When his student Rebbi Eliezer died, he commanded and said, clear the courtyard because of the impurity and prepare a chair for Rabban Joḥanan ben Zakkai. But some say, what his teacher saw, he saw. They proposed marriage into the family of the Patriarch to one of the family Pazi, but he did not accept and said that they should not be ashamed. When he was dying, he commanded and said, clear the courtyard because of the impurity and prepare a chair for Josaphat, the king of Judah. They said, the one who ran after honor<sup class="footnote-marker">284</sup><i class="footnote">While all other Davidic kings married local women, he married a princess from the House of Omri.</i> should come for him who fled before honor.
<sup class="footnote-marker">285</sup><i class="footnote">Cf. Notes 209 ff.</i> Rebbi Jacob bar Idi in the name of Rebbi Joshua ben Levi: It happened that Elders came together in the upper floor of the house Gadia in Jericho, when a disembodied voice came and said to them: There are among you two who would be worthy that the Holy Spirit should rest on them, and one of them is Hillel the Elder. They all looked at Samuel Minor. Again it happened that Elders came together in a second floor at Jabne, when a disembodied voice came and said to them: There are among you two who would be worthy that the Holy Spirit should rest on them, and one of them is Samuel Minor. They all looked at Rebbi Eliezer ben Hyrkanos and were happy that their opinion<sup class="footnote-marker">286</sup><i class="footnote">About Samuel Minor.</i> coincided with that of the Omnipresent.
